   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of countries by suicide rate</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Wikipedia list article
      </div> 
      <p> The following are <b>lists of countries by suicide rate</b> as published by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) and other sources.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[note 1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About one person in 5,000–15,000 dies by <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">suicide</a> every year, with an estimated global rate of 10.5 per 100,000 population<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup> down from 11.6 in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Var2012_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-5">[4]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/High-income" class="mw-redirect" title="High-income">high-income</a> modernised countries male and female rates of suicidal behaviors differ much compared to those in the rest of the world: while women are reportedly more prone to suicidal thoughts, rates of suicide are higher among men (suicide in men has been described as a “silent epidemic”).<sup id="cite_ref-WHO2002_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2002-6">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RouIntHand2016_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RouIntHand2016-8">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EncGenSoc2009_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EncGenSoc2009-9">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BCMJ2011_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BCMJ2011-10">[9]</a></sup> The most suicidal country in the entire world is by a wide margin <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, after its last decades <a href="/wiki/Modernization_theory" title="Modernization theory">modernizing</a> transformation from remote colony to welfare state, with a male-female ratio of 2.99.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Suicide_Capital_of_the_World_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Suicide_Capital_of_the_World-11">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GBD_Results2016_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GBD_Results2016-12">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, of the South Asia <a href="/wiki/WHO_regions" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO regions">region</a>, is the greatest contributor to the absolute number of suicide deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> Europe is the most suicidal region in the world, while the Eastern Mediterranean is the least.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO2015_Crude_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015_Crude-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EuropeHighest_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EuropeHighest-15">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to a recent study, the global rates of suicide death have fallen by a third between 1990 and 2016 if data is asymmetrically adjusted for age, meaning the number of suicides by younger people decreased in particular (even while the absolute number of deaths increased by 6.7%, from 762,000 to 817,000 annually). Worldwide, the rates in 2016 were about 16 deaths per 100,000 men and 7 deaths per 100,000 women: <a href="/wiki/Women" class="mw-redirect" title="Women">women</a> also experienced a greater decrease compared with <a href="/wiki/Men" class="mw-redirect" title="Men">men</a> over the study period.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>In much of the world, suicide is stigmatized and condemned for religious or cultural reasons. In some countries, suicidal behavior is a criminal offence punishable by law. Suicide is therefore often a secretive act surrounded by taboo, and may be unrecognized, misclassified or deliberately hidden in official records of death.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO2002_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2002-6">[5]</a></sup></p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        — <cite>World Health Organization (2002)</cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

           <div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;text-align:center;">

      <p>Male and female suicide rates are out of total male population and total female population, respectively (i.e. total number of male suicides divided by total male population). <a href="/wiki/Age_standardization" class="mw-redirect" title="Age standardization">Age-standardized</a> rates account for the influence that different population age distributions might have on the analysis of crude death rates, statistically addressing the prevailing trends by age-groups and populations' structures, to enhance long term cross-national comparability: based on age-groups' deviation from standardized population structures, rates are rounded up or down (age-adjustment). Basically, the presence of younger individuals in any given age structure carries more weight: if the rate is rounded up that means the <a href="/wiki/Median_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Median age">median age</a> is lower than average for that region (or country), and vice versa when rounded down. </p>
      <p>Most countries listed below report a higher male suicide rate, as worldwide there are about 3 male suicides out of 4, or a factor of 3:1 (for example,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[20]</a></sup> in the United States was 3.36 in 2015, and 3.53 in 2016).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[a]</a></sup> Low population countries are excluded. </p>
      <p>Though age-standardization is common statistical process to categorize mortality data for comparing purposes this approach by WHO is based on estimates which take into account issues such as under-reporting, resulting in rates differing from the official national statistics prepared and endorsed by individual countries (and revisions are also performed periodically). Also, age-adjusted rates are mortality rates that would have existed if all populations under study had the same age distribution as a "standard" population. Plain, crude estimated rates are available at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://apps.who.int/gho/data/view.main.MHSUICIDEREGv?lang=en">here</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ghdx.healthdata.org/gbd-results-tool?params=gbd-api-2017-permalink/ba7956e8e4b44369346f6ca2efa8bc41">here</a>. </p>

      <h2><span id="List_by_other_sources_and_years_.281985.E2.80.932018.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="List_by_other_sources_and_years_(1985–2018)">List by other sources and years (1985–2018)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_suicide_rate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: List by other sources and years (1985–2018)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sucide_rate.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Sucide_rate.PNG/400px-Sucide_rate.PNG" decoding="async" width="400" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Sucide_rate.PNG/600px-Sucide_rate.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Sucide_rate.PNG/800px-Sucide_rate.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1427" data-file-height="628"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sucide_rate.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Suicide rate per 100,000 people by country (1978–2009)<sup id="cite_ref-varnik2012_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-varnik2012-29">[23]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In this list various sources from various years are included, mixing plain crude rates with age-adjusted rates and estimated rates, so cross-national comparability is somewhat skewed. </p> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable" style="text-align: left;"> 
       <caption>
        <b>Suicides per 100,000 people per year</b><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[24]</a></sup> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr style="background:#ececec;"> 
         <th style="text-align:left;" class="unsortable">Regions </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Male </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Female </th> 
         <th data-sort-type="number">Average </th> 
         <th>Year </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_Greenland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Greenland.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_Greenland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Greenland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_Greenland.svg/45px-Flag_of_Greenland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (<a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-NPR.org_2016_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR.org_2016-31">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Suicide_Capital_of_the_World_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Suicide_Capital_of_the_World-11">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rising_suicide_rate_baffles_Greenland_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rising_suicide_rate_baffles_Greenland-32">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GBD_Results2016_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GBD_Results2016-12">[11]</a></sup> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Suicide_in_Greenland" title="Suicide in Greenland">more info</a>)</small></td> 
         <td>84.99</td> 
         <td>28.44</td>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_suicide_rate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The first global estimates on suicide mortality began in the early 1990s, as a single World Bank-commissioned study on general mortality data compiled by the WHO as the first work of its kind on the <a href="/wiki/Global_burden_of_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Global burden of disease">global burden of disease</a> (GBD).<sup id="cite_ref-WHOaboutGBD_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHOaboutGBD-1">[1]</a></sup> In the following years, the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Health_Metrics_and_Evaluation" title="Institute for Health Metrics and Evaluation">Institute for Health Metrics and Evaluation</a> acted as the coordinating center for the study then resulted in the collaboration between several researchers and institutions from many countries.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Data revised in April 2017 and April 2018. Revision for 2015 rates is available at World Health Organization's website, including year 2016 rates.<sup id="cite_ref-CrudeRates_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrudeRates-18">[17]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-nam-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-nam_20-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">To proportion and compare the <i>prevalence</i> of suicide for different countries, WHO adjusts for age (<a href="/wiki/Age_standardization" class="mw-redirect" title="Age standardization">age-standardization</a>) every country's crude mortality rate based on demographic parameters and general mortality data (life expectancy) including other relevant statistical data such as median population ages, sex ratios and age distribution (i.e. age-groups) and its future development, enhancing long term cross-national comparability. Another way to think of it, is that since populations age structures are often very different, but the likelihood of dying by suicide is generally increased with age, in order to avoid masking the sensible differences given by each country's age distributions, countries' rates are reciprocally <a href="/wiki/Weighted" class="mw-redirect" title="Weighted">weighted</a> into the overall trend to globally frame national suicide rates, and the <a href="/wiki/Epidemiological" class="mw-redirect" title="Epidemiological">epidemiological</a> prevalence of suicide. Age-standardization works over time as a measure of the prevalence of suicide across diversely populated countries, by rounding down when populations are composed of a higher percentage of older people compared to the "standard" population, and vice versa.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Europe is the most suicidal region of the world according to crude rates.<sup id="cite_ref-EuropeHighest_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EuropeHighest-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WHO2015_Crude_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015_Crude-14">[13]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In government's annual release, there were 3637 people per one hundred thousands of people in 2018 died of contacting poison, <i>accidental</i> fall, exposure to fire or smoke, <i>accidental</i> drowning including sinking beneath water to death in addition to the suicidal death that was equal to 3865 people per 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-衛生福利部_2019_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-衛生福利部_2019-42">[36]</a></sup> Nevertheless, jumping from a high building as well as drowning were commom methods of suicide in Taiwan,<sup id="cite_ref-Lung_Liao_Wu_Lee_2017_pp._136–143_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lung_Liao_Wu_Lee_2017_pp._136–143-43">[37]</a></sup> indicating the potential risks of <a href="/wiki/Type_I_and_type_II_errors" title="Type I and type II errors">type I and type II errors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Misuse_of_statistics" title="Misuse of statistics">misuse of statistics</a> within the gorvernment's report. Hence, if halves of the death rates of the drowning and fall that were shown in government's report were extracted and added into the self-inflicted deaths (intentional injury death of self), it yields 0.0201% which is thought better reflecting the real case.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Recently released figures by official Belgian authorities suggest a considerably higher rate of 17.0 persons (total) per 100,000 people per annum in 2009 (5,712 cases in a population of 10,749,000 (=10,666,866 as of 1 January 2008 increasing by 0,77% per annum.) as of 1 January 2009).<cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.is/20121205225949/http://www.demorgen.be/dm/nl/5036/Binnenland/article/detail/1216317/2011/02/01/Toenemend-aantal-zelfdodingen-in-Belgie.dhtml">"Toenemend aantal zelfdodingen in Belgie"</a> (in Dutch). 2011. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.demorgen.be/dm/nl/5036/Binnenland/article/detail/1216317/2011/02/01/Toenemend-aantal-zelfdodingen-in-Belgie.dhtml">the original</a> on 5 December 2012.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Toenemend+aantal+zelfdodingen+in+Belgie&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.demorgen.be%2Fdm%2Fnl%2F5036%2FBinnenland%2Farticle%2Fdetail%2F1216317%2F2011%2F02%2F01%2FToenemend-aantal-zelfdodingen-in-Belgie.dhtml&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+countries+by+suicide+rate" class="Z3988"></span><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r982806391">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-free a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-free a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Lock-green.svg")right 0.1em          <li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The number of death in Belgium in 2008 due to suicide "zichzelf schade toebrengen" was reported at 2000 out of a total of 103.760 death. These death comprise 1453 men and 547 women. This puts the suicide rate at about 19 per 100.000. See statbel: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://statbel.fgov.be/nl/binaries/NL%20-%20Tableau%201%2E3_T_2008_tcm325-168456.pdf">http://statbel.fgov.be/nl/binaries/NL%20-%20Tableau%201%2E3_T_2008_tcm325-168456.pdf</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130928160210/http://statbel.fgov.be/nl/binaries/NL%20-%20Tableau%201%2E3_T_2008_tcm325-168456.pdf">Archived</a> 28 September 2013 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-55">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In government's annual release, there were 3637 people per one hundred thousands people in 2018 died of contacting poison, <i>accidental</i> fall, exposure to fire or smoke, <i>accidental</i> drowning, or sinking beneath water that were excluded from the statistical suicidal death figure equal to 3865 people per 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-衛生福利部_2019_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-衛生福利部_2019-42">[36]</a></sup> Furthermore, jumping from a high building as well as drowning were commom methods of suicide in Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-Lung_Liao_Wu_Lee_2017_pp._136–143_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lung_Liao_Wu_Lee_2017_pp._136–143-43">[37]</a></sup></span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>The updated figure of suicide rates in Belgium for 2011 is 2,084 with a total population of 10,933,607, equivalent to 18.96 per 100,000 inhabitants (source: Het Nieuwsblad, 10 April 2014).</li> 
       <li>Taiwan is not a member of the WHO. The Taiwanese government adopted the WHO standard in 2007. According to the Taiwanese government's self-released data, the figure is standardized based upon the population within Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[84]</a></sup></li>
      </ul>

      <ul>
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.who.int/mental_health/prevention/suicide/country_reports/en/index.html">Suicide rates by country, 1950-2011</a> published by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO).</li>
